  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The whole story kept me very engaged and I could never seem to stop reading it, but I absolutely hated the ending of it. It made me really mad and mad<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The whole story kept me very engaged and I could never seem to stop reading it, but I absolutely hated the ending of it. It made me really mad and made me want to throw the book across the room. I really like this book but the ending of it ruined it for me and it bumped my rating for it down because of that.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2609677543?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zainab" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zainab" href="/user/show/48759239-zainab">Zainab</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48759239-zainab?shelf=classic">classic</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2609677543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1416401411248274564">I had aimed to read 40 books this year and this is my 140th so please believe me when I say I am PROUD of myself!<br/>The Outsiders is one of my all time favorite book and I wanted to read something similar so I picked this one up. This one's set around the time as The Outsiders and also has Ponyboy's cameo ( I cannot express how happy I got when I read about him!) <br/>The story's great, the book's great but I will never forgive Bryon for what he did. God, the ending was heartbreaking! <br/>Do yourself a favo</span>
  <span id="freeText1416401411248274564" style="display:none">I had aimed to read 40 books this year and this is my 140th so please believe me when I say I am PROUD of myself!<br />The Outsiders is one of my all time favorite book and I wanted to read something similar so I picked this one up. This one's set around the time as The Outsiders and also has Ponyboy's cameo ( I cannot express how happy I got when I read about him!) <br />The story's great, the book's great but I will never forgive Bryon for what he did. God, the ending was heartbreaking! <br />Do yourself a favour and read this book. It's short, sweet and heartwrenching. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1819311447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8517639880217362950">“You know what the crummiest feeling you can have is? To hate the person you love the best in the world.” <br/>― S.E. Hinton, That Was Then, This Is Now<br/><br/><br/><br/>I read this as a kid but lately certain things have made me think of it and perhaps I will do a reread.<br/><br/>This book is lesser known then "The Outsiders". S.E. Hinton wrote both and I am a huge fan of both these books. While I still prefer The Outsiders, this is a great book as well.<br/><br/>Many are familiar with the plot. Mark and Bryan have been best friends al</span>
  <span id="freeText8517639880217362950" style="display:none">“You know what the crummiest feeling you can have is? To hate the person you love the best in the world.” <br />― S.E. Hinton, That Was Then, This Is Now<br /><br /><br /><br />I read this as a kid but lately certain things have made me think of it and perhaps I will do a reread.<br /><br />This book is lesser known then "The Outsiders". S.E. Hinton wrote both and I am a huge fan of both these books. While I still prefer The Outsiders, this is a great book as well.<br /><br />Many are familiar with the plot. Mark and Bryan have been best friends all their lives. But things are changing. Bryan is changing. He is growing up and for the first time he has a girlfriend. Mark however is not happy with this and wants things to remain just as they have always been.<br /><br />SPOILERS:<br /><br />I related to Mark in this book greatly. Things are always changing..who hasn't wanted, at one point or more, for things to just slow down..or freeze altogether?<br /><br />I am someone who is not all that comfortable with change. And growing up, I too felt this amazing free feeling, the feeling that it would always be this way. This is such an easy book to relate to.<br /><br />FYI..this book was also a film. I saw it and the ending is completely different. It actually ends on a (semi) happy note. I can understand the "Hollywooding" of the ending but honesty, the book's bleak ending is closer to reality and is most likely how it really would have played out.<br /><br />Although I felt for Mark, I do not excuse some of his actions. Likewise, I felt for Bryan, trying to stay afloat in a world that is changing, trying to hold on to both people he loves while dealing with so much.<br /><br />I hope if one has not read this book and they stumble on this review, they will pick it up. Hinton is an incredible writer. She gets in side her characters heads and crafts amazing literature. I've never forgotten this extraordinary book and will reread soon . Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8517639880217362950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3448922688" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3448922688" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26682058-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602529501p2/26682058.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3448922688?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/26682058-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/21064618-that-was-then-this-is-now">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3448922688" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10518072072688233337"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/><i>"It's not just a stage! You can't say 'It's just a stage,' when it's important to people what they're feeling. Maybe he will outgrow it someday, but right <u>now</u> it's important."</i> -- Cathy, on page 104<br/><br/>One of Hinton's strengths as a writer is creating / populating an entire fictional 'wrong side of the tracks' section of real-life Tulsa, Oklahoma (her birthplace / hometown) with a score of well-defined teenagers and/or young adults who are trying their best to navigate their way through mess</span>
  <span id="freeText10518072072688233337" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br /><i>"It's not just a stage! You can't say 'It's just a stage,' when it's important to people what they're feeling. Maybe he will outgrow it someday, but right <u>now</u> it's important."</i> -- Cathy, on page 104<br /><br />One of Hinton's strengths as a writer is creating / populating an entire fictional 'wrong side of the tracks' section of real-life Tulsa, Oklahoma (her birthplace / hometown) with a score of well-defined teenagers and/or young adults who are trying their best to navigate their way through messy and disorganized lives. The succinct <i>That Was Then, This is Now</i> shares lineage with two of Hinton's other books, <i>The Outsiders</i> and <i>Tex</i>, as some of the characters freely jump between or through the stories.<br /><br /><i>That Was Then . . .</i> focuses on and is first-person narrated by Bryon, a fourteen year-old growing up in a single-parent household (somewhat uncommon at the time, way back in the summer of '71) with an 'adopted' brother / best friend of similar age named Mark. The boys engage in a lot of juvenile delinquent or petty criminal activity, but it eventually becomes clear that Bryon - with his crudely thoughtful nature - will potentially mature and possibly grow up / grow out of it. Mark, however, is a different story, and seems to have an undercurrent of unpredictability. The book details how their long-running brotherly bond is strained once events start occurring that firmly push the two boys towards adulthood. I admire that Hinton crafted an ending here that was melancholy, and had one of the characters make a life-altering decision that appears to be divisive to readers. The author again also explores her regular theme (never in a heavy-handed way, but very apparent in her stories) of the importance of a positive male role model - or the problem with the lack thereof - in a boy's life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10518072072688233337" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_553477956" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/553477956" />
    <a title="Jazmin Jade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18087649-jazmin-jade"><img alt="Jazmin Jade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362528993p2/18087649.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/553477956?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jazmin Jade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jazmin Jade" href="/user/show/18087649-jazmin-jade">Jazmin Jade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer553477956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17792092736397573475">This book is heartbreaking. <br/><br/>I read it years ago and wanted to read it again. Want to know the reason why it took me years to read it again? Because I cried my eyes out when I finished it the first time, that it has taken me this long to be able to read it again. The heartbreak was still there when I reached the end, but it was a memory of the original heartbreak. I didn’t cry the second time around, but I was close to it.<br/><br/>The characters are are very well developed making you feel everything they </span>
  <span id="freeText17792092736397573475" style="display:none">This book is heartbreaking. <br /><br />I read it years ago and wanted to read it again. Want to know the reason why it took me years to read it again? Because I cried my eyes out when I finished it the first time, that it has taken me this long to be able to read it again. The heartbreak was still there when I reached the end, but it was a memory of the original heartbreak. I didn’t cry the second time around, but I was close to it.<br /><br />The characters are are very well developed making you feel everything they do, which I dont always find is possible with such short books, but it achieved completely here. It very raw in its emotions, and uncensored in censored kinda way. The lifestyle is one that is brutally harsh and often unpleasant to think about, but the author doesnt stoop to using lots of swear words though there are plenty of occasions when they are walked around. The author leaves the mentions ‘foul’ speak open to interpretation, like she does with just the right amount of the settings and the rest of book. Hinton gives you enough to help form the image she wants, but not enough to wreck the experience of using some of your own imagination. <br /><br />Though by the title name, and the general style that we found from Hinton’s first book The Outsiders (which I will review once I tape my copy back together) we can kind of guess that the story isn’t going to end happily, but what happens is still unexpected and enough to make one cry. <br /><br />A small touch I really enjoyed about this book is that made me enjoy it just that little bit more, the setting is the same from The Outsiders and you get to see a glimpse of the old main character Ponyboy Curtis once again, but he doesnt take over the story. Because of this I recommend that you read the first one before this even though they aren’t related, you might just get that something else out of it.<br /><br />The only bad note I have to say about this book is that there were just a couple of phrases/wording issues that I had to go back and read a couple of times because they didnt flow very. <br /><br />So in conclusion READ THIS BOOK!! Its a great short read that will alter your soul.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17792092736397573475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_909162801" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/909162801" />
    <a title="Irina Elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7664770-irina-elena"><img alt="Irina Elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587303756p2/7664770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/909162801?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irina Elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irina Elena" href="/user/show/7664770-irina-elena">Irina Elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101642597" href="/book/show/17081790-that-was-then-this-is-now">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=ya-realistic">ya-realistic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer909162801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9001910835979024271">See, everyone's talking about how the ending is wonderfully dark and hopeless and brave in its horror.<br/>Well, <i>I</i> think it's bullshit.<br/>I think Mark is gorgeous inside and outside, and fearless and clever and slightly twisted and dead sexy, and I think Bryon is a flighty, selfish, irrational <i>dick</i>. And I'm pissed about it.<br/><br/>You know what I'd love right now? I'd love to have a book about Mark. Just Mark. How he grew up and grew harder, what he felt for Bryon and the rest of the world, his reasons and his </span>
  <span id="freeText9001910835979024271" style="display:none">See, everyone's talking about how the ending is wonderfully dark and hopeless and brave in its horror.<br />Well, <i>I</i> think it's bullshit.<br />I think Mark is gorgeous inside and outside, and fearless and clever and slightly twisted and dead sexy, and I think Bryon is a flighty, selfish, irrational <i>dick</i>. And I'm pissed about it.<br /><br />You know what I'd love right now? I'd love to have a book about Mark. Just Mark. How he grew up and grew harder, what he felt for Bryon and the rest of the world, his reasons and his ways.<br />Bryon? Fuck Bryon. Bryon is the younger, less impactful version of the classic inept middle-aged protagonist who exists just to show the lows humanity can get to or some such thing, and on a scale of one to any other character Hinton has written about he sucks balls, starting around halfway through the book and up until the very end.<br /><br />It's a captivating story, I'll give Hinton that.<br />Brotherhood, friendship and life in the hood are all touched with a delicate hand, and Hinton manages to convey what they mean and feel like without even needing to explicitly <i>tell</i> the reader about them.<br />The great characters counterbalance the awful ones: Mark does it for Bryon, M&amp;M for Cathy. I suppose it all sort of balances out, in the end - but this could have achieved <i>greatness</i>. There are good seeds.<br /><br />Bryon, my man, let me give you some anything-but-friendly advice: TALK IT OUT before you act, or get the fuck outta here.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9001910835979024271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12889109162715899297">Every bit as punching (no pun intended) as The Outsiders, but with a much darker ending. <br/>It was great to see cameos of the characters from The Outsiders. The different perspective on Curtis was a nice touch. <br/><br/>Hinton's writing style made a noticeable improvement. Which is saying a lot.   <span id="freeText12889109162715899297" style="display:none">Every bit as punching (no pun intended) as The Outsiders, but with a much darker ending. <br />It was great to see cameos of the characters from The Outsiders. The different perspective on Curtis was a nice touch. <br /><br />Hinton's writing style made a noticeable improvement. Which is saying a lot. While she was fantastic in The Outsiders, this book made her points a lot more subtle (with the exception of the titled line). She made no great effort to foreshadow events, yet everything fell into a logical line of consequences that can surprise you if you're not anticipating it. I also feel that the personal development of the characters was better portrayed than in The Outsiders. <br />The ending broke my heart and threw out the pieces.<br /><br />Favorite quotes:<br />"If you have two friends in your lifetime, you're lucky. If you have one GOOD friend, you're more than lucky." p. 43<br /><br />"If people think you can't hear them, they talk as if you couldn't. You can hear some pretty neat stuff that way." p. 45 (I do this a lot)<br /><br />"You know what the crummiest feeling you can have is? To hate the person you love the best in the world." p. 49<br /><br />'Nothing can wear you out like caring for people." p. 139</span>

<div id="review_281795197" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/281795197" />
    <a title="Licha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5614272-licha"><img alt="Licha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337135662p2/5614272.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/281795197?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Licha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Licha" href="/user/show/5614272-licha">Licha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614272-licha?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614272-licha?shelf=favorite-author">favorite-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614272-licha?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614272-licha?shelf=read-more-than-once">read-more-than-once</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614272-licha?shelf=childhood-fave">childhood-fave</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer281795197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6550792352956943276">My 12yr old self would have probably given this 5 stars. But "that was then, this is now". <--Pun, pun. Lol. Sorry, that was pretty bad. I couldn't help it.<br/><br/>Let's just say this was not meant to have been read by my way older self. This was pretty bad, and I'm only giving this 2 stars because nostalgia and S.E. Hinton and The Outsiders.<br/><br/>The characters are unlikable and I do remember not liking them even back when I was younger. Bryon thinks he's cool, and a know it all, but he really has no clue he</span>
  <span id="freeText6550792352956943276" style="display:none">My 12yr old self would have probably given this 5 stars. But "that was then, this is now". &lt;--Pun, pun. Lol. Sorry, that was pretty bad. I couldn't help it.<br /><br />Let's just say this was not meant to have been read by my way older self. This was pretty bad, and I'm only giving this 2 stars because nostalgia and S.E. Hinton and The Outsiders.<br /><br />The characters are unlikable and I do remember not liking them even back when I was younger. Bryon thinks he's cool, and a know it all, but he really has no clue he's not a likable guy. He falls for Cathy and immediately is choosing her over Mark, his brother from another mother. There's never enough detail about Cathy and what makes her so special. If anything, she's also dislikable. I think I liked Angela better, a girl from the bad side of the tracks who Bryon used to date. What's so special about Cathy that makes Bryon be disloyal to Mark? Yeah, didn't care enough about these two.<br /><br />Some other peeves with this book:<br /><br />--I hate the way Bryon's name was spelled? Small detail, but it bugged me throughout the whole book.<br /><br />--After Charlie's death, the police decide to give Bryon and Mark Charlie's car because "they think Charlie would have wanted them to have it", although Bryon and Mark are not related to Charlie. This was very sloppy writing. Like yeah, I wish someone would decide I could have something because I had that needy look.<br /><br />--Ponyboy (of The Outsiders) appears throughout the book. In my opinion, he should have been kept out of this story. <br /><br />--The ending was terrible. If I disliked Bryon at the start, I really hated him by the end. And then there's the absentee mom, who finally appears, only to make Bryon feel like he made the right decision.<br /><br />I hate to rate this so low. S.E. Hinton was one of my favorite authors growing up. I read, and reread, and reread The Outsiders. I guess I was expecting the same magic for this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6550792352956943276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2797871348049287652">WHAT THE HECK WAS THAT !!!!!!!!! I had to read The Outsiders for class and had the option of reading That Was Then, This is Now for an assignment, which I decided to do since The Outsiders is great and I'll probably never read this book if I don't now. First off the synopsis the book gives you is a lie, what Byron discovers is in the very last chapter of the book! The real small summary was that a boy named Mark lives with Byron and Byron's mom. Byron and Mark hustle at poker frequently and mana</span>
  <span id="freeText2797871348049287652" style="display:none">WHAT THE HECK WAS THAT !!!!!!!!! I had to read The Outsiders for class and had the option of reading That Was Then, This is Now for an assignment, which I decided to do since The Outsiders is great and I'll probably never read this book if I don't now. First off the synopsis the book gives you is a lie, what Byron discovers is in the very last chapter of the book! The real small summary was that a boy named Mark lives with Byron and Byron's mom. Byron and Mark hustle at poker frequently and manage to be friends with the owner of the building. Byron meets a girl named Cathy who he's smitten by but Mark can't stand her. But when something unfortunate happens to the owner of the poker place, opinions on the world are changed, Mark seams to live in the moment and sorta doesn't care and is much less sad while Byron thinks it's all his fault and feels awful for it!<br /><br />GRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR The book itself isn't captivating but THE ENDING!!!!!!!! The book if it didn't have the ending it does would've probably been a three there isn't truly a moment I'm on the edge of my seat, but how much drama can you expect from a short story? But the ending is completely miserable and frankly I've given up on having perfect endings and I'm done being bother by them..... THIS WAS THE EXCEPTION, I MEAN I CAN'T SPOIL IT BUT.... nothing's resolved and he practically has a breakdown at the very last chapter</span>
  <a data-text-id="2797871348049287652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/434940229?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/10520669-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer434940229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15276218345901409748">This was another joint read with my daughter. She was pleased to see the reappearance of Ponyboy, but would have liked to have seen a bit more of him. It was fun to discuss with her the similarities and then contrast the differences of Bryon and Ponyboy. Both were intelligent, got good grades, were from the poor side of town scraping to make ends meet, and clearly had good morals; pretty much. Yet unlike Ponyboy, Bryon is a player with the girls, self-assured and a risk taker. To be sure, they a</span>
  <span id="freeText15276218345901409748" style="display:none">This was another joint read with my daughter. She was pleased to see the reappearance of Ponyboy, but would have liked to have seen a bit more of him. It was fun to discuss with her the similarities and then contrast the differences of Bryon and Ponyboy. Both were intelligent, got good grades, were from the poor side of town scraping to make ends meet, and clearly had good morals; pretty much. Yet unlike Ponyboy, Bryon is a player with the girls, self-assured and a risk taker. To be sure, they are older now and Ponyboy has likely matured. But at the last read, his self-image was weak and he was only just starting to believe in himself, his story. <br /><br />Hailey hated the ending. And was surprised when I told her this was <em>good</em>. This was life, reality, and that whether or not we like it change happens. We're <strong>supposed</strong> to hate the ending. Change, for the most part, is supposed to make us uncomfortable at times, but it's how we adapt to us that helps us grow and learn as people. I love reading with my daughter and hope to continue with stories like these for years to come. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15276218345901409748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13770551060408499168">It really is amazing to me that this author, a female, can get into the head of a male teenager, to such a degree that she so completely reveals his thoughts, his actions, his justifications, his excuses, etc. In reading about the author, she said that as a teen she was not satisfied with what was available for her to read so she did something about it and as a consequence she wrote literature relevant to and for a young adult audience. (Of course, the frankness and bold honesty over the years h</span>
  <span id="freeText13770551060408499168" style="display:none">It really is amazing to me that this author, a female, can get into the head of a male teenager, to such a degree that she so completely reveals his thoughts, his actions, his justifications, his excuses, etc. In reading about the author, she said that as a teen she was not satisfied with what was available for her to read so she did something about it and as a consequence she wrote literature relevant to and for a young adult audience. (Of course, the frankness and bold honesty over the years has not been so completely embraced and her books have been "taught in some schools and banned in others".) Her target audience may be YA, but I contend that adults can also learn from and benefit from the honest dialogue of teens who are growing up in near poverty situations so that rather than reacting with judgement there can be an attempt for a deeper understanding.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10962596763490853889">I think I've read <u>The Outsiders</u> at least 6 times but strangely I've never read any other of Hinton's books until now. I picked this one up at the library for $1 and I'm very glad I did. It's just as gritty and real as Outsiders but it's time period is set a bit later.   <span id="freeText10962596763490853889" style="display:none">I think I've read <u>The Outsiders</u> at least 6 times but strangely I've never read any other of Hinton's books until now. I picked this one up at the library for $1 and I'm very glad I did. It's just as gritty and real as Outsiders but it's time period is set a bit later. (Not too late for Ponyboy to make a cameo appearance though.It's fun even reading that name!) As a parent of a teenager and more on their way there it was a good reminder of all the crazy emotions of that age. My favorite part is Cathy crying to her father and saying, "You can't say, 'This is just a stage,' when it's important to people what they're feeling. Maybe he will outgrow it someday, but right <i>now</i> it's important." Loved it!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_743643449" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/743643449" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12248943-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499990463p2/12248943.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/743643449?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/12248943-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer743643449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17989763485965101359"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/231804.The_Outsiders' title='The Outsiders by S.E. Hinton' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Outsiders</a> is one of the most important books in YA history. I doubt it was the first book to portray poverty and gang violence among teenagers realistically, but it was the first to get popular, and it hugely expanded the boundaries of what books for kids could do, in a way that's never been done before or since. With The Outsiders, Hinton paved the way for authors who took teenagers seriously as an audience to write about important issues. Do you like books like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22628.The_Perks_of_Being_a_Wallflower' title='The Perks of Being a Wallflower by Stephen Chbosky' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Perks of Being a Wallf</a></span>
  <span id="freeText17989763485965101359" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/231804.The_Outsiders" title="The Outsiders by S.E. Hinton" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Outsiders</a> is one of the most important books in YA history. I doubt it was the first book to portray poverty and gang violence among teenagers realistically, but it was the first to get popular, and it hugely expanded the boundaries of what books for kids could do, in a way that's never been done before or since. With The Outsiders, Hinton paved the way for authors who took teenagers seriously as an audience to write about important issues. Do you like books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22628.The_Perks_of_Being_a_Wallflower" title="The Perks of Being a Wallflower by Stephen Chbosky" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Perks of Being a Wallflower</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Fault in Our Stars</a>? Well, they wouldn't be possible without Hinton's influence. Books can be influential without being good, but I'm happy to say that I did moderately enjoy The Outsiders. It had its flaws, but it's a solid YA book, especially considering that Hinton was doing something she'd essentially never seen done before. So it made sense that it would be good to check out her follow-up. This book didn't have the same popularity that The Outsiders did, but I still see it in used bookstores every once in a while.<br /><br />But, unfortunately, this turned out to be a far weaker book than The Outsiders. I can see why this book wasn't as popular or acclaimed as The Outsiders - it's just not as impactful or well-written.<br /><br />The first problem is immediately irritating, from the opening pages of the book: the direct characterization. Bryon is <i>constantly</i> telling us things about the other characters, rather than letting us see for ourselves. This telling, rather than showing, is essentially how every character in the novel is constructed. It got to the point where I'm not even sure if these characters are at all developed - perhaps they just have a lot of informed traits. It gets difficult to tell when Hinton feels the need to inform us of every single thing about them. This device isn't just a lazy way out of using subtlety, it's also an active barrier to letting us connect to these characters. There's no way for a character to feel like a real person when their character traits are being constantly shoved down our throats. Characterization just doesn't work that way. Allowing the reader to do some work in picking up on character traits is essential in keeping the reader engaged - without that, there's no reason for the reader to stay interested.<br /><br />It doesn't help that the plot is so meandering and flimsy. There's no overarching conflict here, just a bunch of barely-related plot threads. Each of the plot threads - Bryon's mom being in the hospital, M&amp;M disappearing, Mark's former girlfriend trying to start a fight, just to name a few - but they don't come together until the very end, and even then, it's very cheap and forced. There's just no forward motion behind this book. The characterization doesn't provide it, and neither does the plot. There's no real tension, no buildup to any sort of real or emotional climax. Things in this book kind of just happen, often never to be brought up again. Hinton just doesn't seem to have a good idea of what she wants to say here. Many of the plot threads have potential themes that could arise from them, but there's no one idea that unites the whole book. That's probably the biggest strength that The Outsiders has compared to this novel. In The Outsiders, Hinton knew exactly what she wanted to say, and everything in the novel built up to that set of ideas. Here, Hinton has no idea what she wants to say, so she has nothing to build the novel around. That's why it ends up so cheap and flimsy.<br /><br />This isn't a horrible novel. Bryon's voice is functionally identical to Ponyboy's, but it at least makes the setting feel immersive. And Hinton definitely does write dialogue well, even if it feels extremely dated today. But there's not much reason to read this novel. It's both far less influential and not nearly as good as The Outsiders, so just go ahead and read that instead of wasting your time here.<br /><br /><b>This review can also be found <a href="http://thelowercasegimmick.tumblr.com/post/139382641016/ya-review-12715-that-was-then-this-is-now-by" rel="nofollow noopener">on my blog</a>.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17989763485965101359" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203001064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3808253030191184828">Do you like gangs, drugs and hustling for money? Well then you’ll love this book. This book is about the criminal life of 16 year old Bryon. Bryon and his best friend Mark used to spend most of their time pool hustling and mugging people. Ever since they were kids they loved to fight. Almost every day they would mug people or hustle them in pool for money. One night that completely changed for Bryon. Their good friend Charlie ran the bar they would hustle in. One night when Bryon and Mark were l</span>
  <span id="freeText3808253030191184828" style="display:none">Do you like gangs, drugs and hustling for money? Well then you’ll love this book. This book is about the criminal life of 16 year old Bryon. Bryon and his best friend Mark used to spend most of their time pool hustling and mugging people. Ever since they were kids they loved to fight. Almost every day they would mug people or hustle them in pool for money. One night that completely changed for Bryon. Their good friend Charlie ran the bar they would hustle in. One night when Bryon and Mark were leaving Charlie’s bar they got called into an ally. Charlie came to the rescue just in time but got shot. Now for Bryon, the thug life doesn’t seem so appealing. The two friends stop seeing each other and begin to grow apart. This book grabbed me from the first page and drove me to read more. S.E. Hinton did a great job with suspense and twists.</span>

<div id="review_24054565" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24054565" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1223946-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1213024223p2/1223946.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24054565?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/1223946-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24054565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10848465014256606617">This is a coming of age story about two best friends, and what happens to them when they start to mature and grow apart. It is a story about friendship, loyalty, and mostly how the difference between right and wrong is subjective. There is excellent character development, and although the book is short (I finished it in a few hours) by the end you feel for every character in the story, as if you really know them. Recommended for anyone who liked The Outsiders.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11083107088043341514" style="display:none">This book is about a guy named Bryon. He lives with his mom and his best friend Mark, lives with him cause both of marks parents died. Mark and Bryon have been best friend way before Mark moved in. One day Bryon had a really bad headache and wanted a cigarette. Mark told Bryon that he could've stopped if he didn't want him to sell them. But it was to late for Mark to do anything now,he can hear the siren beside their house. One day in jail, Bryon went to visit Mark, and mark said"I'm glad your here...so I can tell you that I hate you" This part made me cry so much and:'( I can never forget what happened after and before that.               <span id="reviewTextContainer135481736" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10681035311316491353">The book was so good...during the pages. During the journey of Bryon and Mark, that is. It was emotional, breathtaking, and shocking! S.E. Hinton is an obvious gifted writer, I'll tell anyone! <br/><br/>Bryon is a kid who's focused on the big picture. He's serious but has fun if it's hassling or just being the cool kid. He's a wise-crack kid and the biggest player in Tulsa. He never says "I love you" with feeling. But that was until Cathy came along.<br/><br/>Mark is the joker.   <span id="freeText10681035311316491353" style="display:none">The book was so good...during the pages. During the journey of Bryon and Mark, that is. It was emotional, breathtaking, and shocking! S.E. Hinton is an obvious gifted writer, I'll tell anyone! <br /><br />Bryon is a kid who's focused on the big picture. He's serious but has fun if it's hassling or just being the cool kid. He's a wise-crack kid and the biggest player in Tulsa. He never says "I love you" with feeling. But that was until Cathy came along.<br /><br />Mark is the joker. He's the one who can hardly speak a sentence with out grinning like Two-Bit (character from The Outsiders). He's a 'lion' with blond hair and golden eyes. He's someone who focuses on the moment but will does this help?<br /><br />They've been together for almost ever. Now, that relationship is breaking slowly, crack by crack. Secrets pull them apart, realizations bring them back with anger, and brilliant words connect them. With Bryon growing up and Mark longing to be in the past, can they be best friends? Can they be even friends? This novel keeps you gasping in a total of 11 chapters until the last page.<br /><br />And it's the last page that shocks you the most. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10681035311316491353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Phil Jensen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phil Jensen" href="/user/show/14413650-phil-jensen">Phil Jensen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14413650-phil-jensen?shelf=novel-length-read-in-2017">novel-length-read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2216785646" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2851133440311229464">In her afterward, Hinton mentions that this book was written while fighting through writer's block. It shows. The character dynamics and plot development are very forced and after school special-ish. The characters and situations are dated and awkward. Overall, this is an overrated book that scores some cheap fan points through a cameo by Ponyboy.</span>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2545262446" />
    <a title="Ian Ochieng" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87150262-ian-ochieng"><img alt="Ian Ochieng" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573645417p2/87150262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2545262446?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian Ochieng" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian Ochieng" href="/user/show/87150262-ian-ochieng">Ian Ochieng</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2545262446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18036891016470041494">That Was Then, This Is Now was a very eye opening read that becomes more exciting from the start to the end. <br/><br/> It’s a novel about two boys named Bryon and Mark that are living in a society where their lives can change in the blink of an eye, and Bryon has to start making strong decisions because of Mark’s choices.<br/><br/>I like Bryon, because the more he has life long experiences, the more he starts to realize reality. As the story develops Mark realizes how people really are. Mark learns that just becau</span>
  <span id="freeText18036891016470041494" style="display:none">That Was Then, This Is Now was a very eye opening read that becomes more exciting from the start to the end. <br /><br /> It’s a novel about two boys named Bryon and Mark that are living in a society where their lives can change in the blink of an eye, and Bryon has to start making strong decisions because of Mark’s choices.<br /><br />I like Bryon, because the more he has life long experiences, the more he starts to realize reality. As the story develops Mark realizes how people really are. Mark learns that just because you may be close with someone in the past that they can change to be completely different people later on. He begins to realize that although Mark is his brother that he is a bad influence. Bryon says “He could have talked all night and I wouldn’t have changed my mind. This was wrong.”(141-142). Bryon also says “Mark had absolutely no concept of what was right and what was wrong; he didn’t obey any laws, because he couldn’t see that there were any. Laws, right and wrong, they didn’t matter to Mark, because they were just words.”(142). This shows that Bryon is starting to realize how the world really is, and that people may not who they really seem they are. <br /><br />I enjoyed seeing Bryon grow as a person, and to stop being blinded of the stereotypes of the world he lives in. I would recommend this book to people that enjoy reading about realizations of what the world is really like.<br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7741719922376321440" style="display:none"><br />I liked That Was Then, This is Now because it gives a good, vivid idea on how society was in the 1970’s. 16 yr old Bryon is having a rough time in this book about how hard it was in the 1970’s for some people and Bryon goes through a lot.<br />Bryon goes through a lot of things, especially for a teenager, and he changes his ways tremendously. Bryon experiences a lot of things like, gang violence, death, and depression. <br />Bryon is a good character to display what went on in that society. Bryon starts off the book as a carefree teenager who seems to be living his life but that changes all of a sudden when he goes through a midlife crisis. He experiences one of his friends dying, he also experiences his friend Mark get hit in the face with a bottle which caused a lot of bleeding. The thing that really changed Mark was him seeing M&amp;M messed up and when he sent his best friend to jail. <br />Bryon went from a carefree teenager into a depressed extra-cautious man who didn’t think it would ever get better for him. <br />I recommend this book to people who like books about how the old days were and what the struggle was like for some people.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2009341736" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2009341736" />
    <a title="Kim Clifton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27894457-kim-clifton"><img alt="Kim Clifton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437511357p2/27894457.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2009341736?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim Clifton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim Clifton" href="/user/show/27894457-kim-clifton">Kim Clifton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2009341736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer527927091590455931">An angst-ridden coming of age story about growing apart. <br/><br/>It's almost impossible not to compare this to The Outsiders because it's set in the same town and Ponyboy and the Shepard brothers make appearances. Since most of the story actually takes place in town, it feels like a snapshot of the culture in the 1960s, more so than The Outsiders. On one hand, it's interesting to see how the Socs and Greasers have changed since The Outsiders (props to SE Hinton for the still-timely observation that rich</span>
  <span id="freeText527927091590455931" style="display:none">An angst-ridden coming of age story about growing apart. <br /><br />It's almost impossible not to compare this to The Outsiders because it's set in the same town and Ponyboy and the Shepard brothers make appearances. Since most of the story actually takes place in town, it feels like a snapshot of the culture in the 1960s, more so than The Outsiders. On one hand, it's interesting to see how the Socs and Greasers have changed since The Outsiders (props to SE Hinton for the still-timely observation that rich folk spend a lot of money trying to dress poor), but the characters aren't as kind as the Curtis brothers, so I didn't care about them too much. Bryon's narration sounds a lot like Ponyboy's... until he makes reductive comments about picking up chicks, and it gets annoying. <br /><br />Overall, the book attempts to ponder why bad things happen to good people. It's a fine question, but I'm not sure the way Hinton went about illustrating it is the most effective. The book feels like Bryon and Mark walking through a series of examples and then talking about them philosophically-ish. It's a little forced for a short book to span an entire year, but zoom in only on these conversations. <br /><br />In her author's note, Hinton writes that The Outsiders was to make people feel, and this book is to make people think. Well, mission accomplished, I just think I like feeling better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="527927091590455931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2209565957" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2209565957" />
    <a title="Katy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8979057-katy"><img alt="Katy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588381474p2/8979057.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2209565957?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katy" href="/user/show/8979057-katy">Katy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8979057-katy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8979057-katy?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2209565957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4606852791166825204">S.E. Hinton said this about That Was Then, This Is Now: "The Outsiders made you feel. That Was Then, This Is Now will make you think." That could not be more true. I feel and love and cry over Ponyboy and his story, however, I want to question, analyze, and interrogate Bryon and Mark about their stories. I know others didn't particularly like how Pony was portrayed in this story, but I think it's good he was included to keep those who loved The Outsiders so much reading another book. You get so </span>
  <span id="freeText4606852791166825204" style="display:none">S.E. Hinton said this about That Was Then, This Is Now: "The Outsiders made you feel. That Was Then, This Is Now will make you think." That could not be more true. I feel and love and cry over Ponyboy and his story, however, I want to question, analyze, and interrogate Bryon and Mark about their stories. I know others didn't particularly like how Pony was portrayed in this story, but I think it's good he was included to keep those who loved The Outsiders so much reading another book. You get so focused on Ponyboy and his gang, you forget there could be so many other characters leading similar (or maybe not so similar) lives. <br /><br />I don't think all the references to drugs are appropriate for young readers, but historically speaking, it's accurate for the setting (both time and place). I almost want to teach this book as well because there is SO much to analyze. I really did like it though and will probably read it again to see what I take away with a second reading. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4606852791166825204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161716913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7684687292069520092">This is the story of a cool guy who turns into a total square and narcs his best friend out to the cops. It is infuriating. <br/>It does, however, have Ponyboy Curtis in it and there aren't any vampires.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2531614182" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2531614182" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4014393-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578190142p2/4014393.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2531614182?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/4014393-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jason by: </span>
      Nobody
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4014393-jason?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4014393-jason?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4014393-jason?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2531614182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8530882420057627648">I like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/566772233' title='my review' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Outsiders</a> more, but Ms. Hinton shows us with her second book that she can, indeed, stay gold. And I'll admit that this is the better written book. She improves a lot between ages 16 and 20, but some of the minor annoyances are still there. And I loved the story in this one; just look at all the stars I gave it. But there's a special place in my heart for <i>The Outsiders</i> mostly due to the movie, and that's that. And how awesome is it that Ponyboy makes a brief appearance in this? Uber aw</span>
  <span id="freeText8530882420057627648" style="display:none">I like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/566772233" title="my review" rel="nofollow noopener">The Outsiders</a> more, but Ms. Hinton shows us with her second book that she can, indeed, stay gold. And I'll admit that this is the better written book. She improves a lot between ages 16 and 20, but some of the minor annoyances are still there. And I loved the story in this one; just look at all the stars I gave it. But there's a special place in my heart for <i>The Outsiders</i> mostly due to the movie, and that's that. And how awesome is it that Ponyboy makes a brief appearance in this? Uber awesome! The dude's cool as a fan.<br><br>But this isn't about Ponyboy. It's about Bryon and Mark, besties who grow apart. Once Bryon started moving toward adulthood, I could barely put the book down. I understand him completely. I understand his feelings and turmoil. I understand his decisions (not that I would've made the same ones). I understand his eventual apathy. I understand his "just let me get the fuck away from here" attitude that's implied at the end. And yet I also understand Mark, though he's quite different from Byron. At least I understand part of Mark. I understand the hate, and I'm well acquainted with wanting to hold a grudge. For some people, not holding a grudge comes naturally. For me it takes a lot of work. My natural inclination is to despise the mahfah to the end of his days, and Mark was betrayed pretty severely. But I understand. Yet I also don't like it. I'm quite conflicted, but I'm not pissed off about it at all. Does any of this make sense? If so, you're doing better than me, because I can't make heads or tails of it myself. All I know is that I related to a lot of what was going on, and I loved reading this. S.E. Hinton can make some great characters, and just like with <i>The Outsiders</i>, it's the characters that drive the story and not vice versa. That's my kind of yarn, right there.<br><br>There are strange inconsistencies in this book, but I wouldn't change anything about it since Ms. Hinton seems to be prudish in the same areas that I am. There's violence ranging from minor rough-housing to murder. There's drug use to the point of brain damage. There's drinking to the point of intoxication. There's cigarette smoking. And all of this stuff is happening with 13-16 year-olds. Yet there's no profanity outside of an occasional hell or damn, and rough language is even commented on by our protagonists. There's also a lot of going out with chicks, but it all stops waaaaaaay short of sex, though I reckon it's implied. One minor character thought she was pregnant at one point, but you have to read between the lines to catch that. This came out in 1971, and was made for the young adult genre, so I suppose you could get only so graphic, but I found all of this kind of cute. I think there was some naivety on Hinton's part at work here, but I could be wrong.<br><br>And speaking of naivety, it's funny watching hippies infiltrate Tulsa when a couple of years prior it was just greasers and preps. (At least I assume we're still in Tulsa, OK since Ponyboy was there, and I'm pretty sure that's where <i>The Outsiders</i> was set.) There were small comments throughout on how peaceful the hippies are, and then we get one line from Bryon about how they wouldn't even fight to defend themselves...<br><br><a href="https://imgur.com/WUVinTv" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1537325110ra/26321499.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Redline it, baby. Such a line could be used to describe M&amp;M, a pretty cool hippie character that I actually liked, but Bryon was applying it to all of hippiedom, and I really think that was just an extension of Hinton's actual beliefs. Again, I could be wrong.<br><br>If you like a good coming of age story with a rather sad ending (at least for a young adult book), then get at it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8530882420057627648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2816579318" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2816579318" />
    <a title="Lee Foust" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13984676-lee-foust"><img alt="Lee Foust" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442875445p2/13984676.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2816579318?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee Foust" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee Foust" href="/user/show/13984676-lee-foust">Lee Foust</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2816579318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10185187008342562048">So I'm looking at my lit mag/writer-centered twitter feed sometime last year or the year before and I see an article about S. E. Hinton speaking before an audience. During the Q & A session a fan asks her why she had to kill off the hero of her first and most famous novel and she responds, "Because I'm a stone-cold bitch." Which is, I think, probably the coolest, most honest, and in-your-face answer to a question that any writer has ever given about their work.<br/><br/>I fall back into memories of my ear</span>
  <span id="freeText10185187008342562048" style="display:none">So I'm looking at my lit mag/writer-centered twitter feed sometime last year or the year before and I see an article about S. E. Hinton speaking before an audience. During the Q &amp; A session a fan asks her why she had to kill off the hero of her first and most famous novel and she responds, "Because I'm a stone-cold bitch." Which is, I think, probably the coolest, most honest, and in-your-face answer to a question that any writer has ever given about their work.<br /><br />I fall back into memories of my early teen years in the mid-1970s. A precocious reader enamored of late-night Saturday horror film re-runs, I remember the 4th grade English project we had to do of choosing three somehow thematically-related novels and making a book box to put them in. I chose <i>Dracula</i>, <i>Frankenstein</i>, and <i>The Strange Case of Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde</i>. I remember being more scared to pass my choices by the teacher than I'd ever been by any of the so-called scary films I'd ever seen, feeling like the world--read: my parents--considered monsters to be merely stupid kid stuff. The teacher, Lee Kinser--a wonderful lady (although I did get teased quite a bit because of how much we liked each other and because we had the same first name despite our binary opposed genders)--realizing the literary worth of those three masterpieces, was both impressed and supportive of my choices. I made a hearse out of a shoe box with which to house my little Gothic gems on their way to the cemetery.<br /><br />This is all just to explain how, despite my perfect age for it, I missed out on reading the tough teenage novels of S. E. Hinton back in the day when all of my peers were gobbling them up and feeling cooler-than-cool for doing so. (Yeah, I grew up in an almost totally white upper-middle class suburb where rebellious teenage urges could only yearn for the street fighting, smoking, and general lower-class roughness that her Tulsa novels describe. I, being a product of the working-class uncomfortably inserted into this world through the charm and good luck of my wanna-be bourgeois father wasn't very interested in that stuff at the time.)<br /><br />But, having read the "stone-cold bitch" comment I was intrigued and, finding a copy of <i>That Was Then, This Is Now</i> in a thrift store for a dime, my fate was sealed.<br /><br />I enjoyed it. Even at my age--mid fifties--I was not at all immune to the novel's narrative of the anxieties and traumas inevitable as one moves from childlike self-absorption to an adult awareness of others, empathy, and feelings of responsibility. Along with this perhaps rather obvious truth, the novel even goes deeper by showing how to discover love is also to discover jealousy and how emotions kind of inevitably lead to a sort of bi-polar experience of agony and ecstasy for which young people are scarcely equipped to deal when they first encounter these seemingly contradictory emotions. And, while we get better at it with practice, the pleasures and pains of love, of caring about almost anything, never totally goes away. So, yeah, it's a novel for adolescents of all ages.<br /><br />My biggest beef with the novel, though, is the narrator's constantly having to skirt around all of the bad language that various characters use during the course of the narrative. Doing so kept reminding me of the writer manipulating the text and her own outward concerns with an audience of teens and the publishing world, which, in those moments, kept getting in the way of the novel's otherwise sincere attempts at telling difficult truths as honestly as possible. But, well, Hinton did a pretty good job of making it feel as if the narrator was making the decision to censor his reality most of the time--but it just happened so much it wasn't always convincing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10185187008342562048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LGD3zPH2/0RbLsBB3+HjVvspgHYOvQKNYv+mXZFrQdoWRp4eSqg2LPwFdCAoFOmJLXZnvsAwjOo5geDsXCizQA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

Hinton, who wrote this modern classic when she was 16 years old, comments: &quot;The Outsiders, like most things I write, is written from a boy\'s point of view. That\'s why I\'m listed as S.E. Hinton rather than Susan. (I figured most boys would look at the book and think \'What can a chick know about stuff like that!\') None of the events are taken from life, but the rest—how kids think and live and feel—is for real. The characters—Dallas, who wasn\'t tough enough; Sodapop, the happy-go-lucky dropout; Bob, the rich kid whose arrogance cost him his life; Ponyboy, the sensitive, green-eyed Greaser who didn\'t want to be a hood—they\'re all real to me. Many of my friends are Greasers, but I\'m not. I have friends who are rich, too, but nobody will ever call me a Soc—I\'ve seen what money and too much idle time and parental approval can do to people. Cool people mean nothing to me—they\'re living behind masks and I\'m always wondering &quot;Is there a real person underneath?&quot; This entirely practical stage adaptation deals with real people, seen through the eyes of young Ponyboy, a Greaser on the wrong side of life, caught up in territorial battles between the have-it-made rich kids—the Socs—and his tough, underprivileged &quot;greaser&quot; family and friends. In the midst of urban warfare, somehow Ponyboy can\'t forget a short poem that speaks of their fragile young lives:\n\nNature\'s first green is gold, Her hardest hue to hold.\nHer early leaf\'s a flower; But only so an hour.\nThen leaf subsides to leaf. So Eden sank to grief,\nso dawn goes down to day. Nothing gold can stay.\n\n&quot;Robert Frost wrote it,&quot; Ponyboy tells Johnny. &quot;I always remembered it because I never quite got what he meant by it.&quot; Cherry, a beautiful Soc, comes to share a special sensitivity with Ponyboy as she discovers that he remembers poems and needs to watch sunsets. At the same time, Cherry\'s attracted to the older, tougher Dallas, and in a sense she\'s caught in the violent space between the Greasers and the Socs. While the Socs appear to have everything, the only thing a Greaser has is his friends. As these young people try to find themselves and each other, as the sadness of sophistication begins to reach them and their battles and relationships reach a resolution, Ponyboy\'s dying friend, Johnny, sends him a last message … I\'ve been thinking about the poem that guy wrote. He meant you\'re gold when you\'re a kid, like green. When you\'re a kid everything\'s new, dawn. It\'s just when you get used to everything that it\'s day. Like the way you dig sunsets, Pony. That\'s gold. Keep it that way. It\'s a good way to be. This is a play about young people who are not yet hopeless about latent decency in the midst of struggle. Area staging.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/762707.S_E_Hinton">About S.E. Hinton</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/762707.S_E_Hinton"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1206505616p3/762707.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/762707.S_E_Hinton">S.E. Hinton

5,459
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11890961863944063317">S.E. Hinton, was and still is, one of the most popular and best known writers of young adult fiction. Her books have been taught in some schools, and banned from others. Her novels changed the way people look at young adult literature. <br/><br/>Susan Eloise Hinton was born in Tulsa, Oklahoma. She has always enjoyed reading but wasn't satisfied with the literature that was being written for young adults, wh</span>
  <span id="freeText11890961863944063317" style="display:none">S.E. Hinton, was and still is, one of the most popular and best known writers of young adult fiction. Her books have been taught in some schools, and banned from others. Her novels changed the way people look at young adult literature. <br /><br />Susan Eloise Hinton was born in Tulsa, Oklahoma. She has always enjoyed reading but wasn't satisfied with the literature that was being written for young adults, which influenced her to write novels like <i>The Outsiders</i>. That book, her first novel, was published in 1967 by Viking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11890961863944063317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
